20#include <stdint.h>
21#include "ksc5601.h"
22
23/*
24egrep '# HANGUL SYLL' < /cdrom/unix/mappings/eastasia/ksc/ksc5601.txt | \
25egrep -v '^0x[4-9AD-F]' | egrep -v '^0x..([4-9].|A0)' | \
26perl tab21.pl > ksc_hangul1.tb
27
28----------
29 $n=0;
30 while (<>) {
31 local($ksc, $ucs4, %rest) = split;
32 local($u)=hex($ucs4);
33 local($k)=hex($ksc);
34 printf ("\n ") if ($n % 8 eq 0);
35 ++$n;
36 printf (" 0x%04x,", $u);
37 }
38 printf ("\n");
39---------
40
41 2350 Hangul syllables defined in KS C 5601 are assigned
42 row 16 - row 40 (with each row having 94 pre-composed syllables).
43
44 No gap exists and all of them are sorted in Unicode 2.0 in the same
45 order as in KS C 5601 so that we can use the single table to convert
46 between KS C 5601-1987 based encodings(EUC-KR, ISO-2022-KR)
47 and UCS-4.
48
49*/
50
51

350/* Mapping table between symbols defined in KS C 5601-1992
351 and UCS-4. It's used to convert symbols in EUC-KR, ISO-2022-KR,
352 Johab, UHC to UCS-4.
353
354egrep '^0xA[1-C]' < /cdrom/unix/mappings/eastasia/ksc/ksc5601.txt | \
355grep -v '# HANGUL SYLLABLE' | perl tab11.pl > ksc_sym1.tb
356
357 $n=0;
358 while (<>) {
359 local($ksc, $ucs4, %rest) = split;
360 local($u)=hex($ucs4);
361 local($k)=hex($ksc);
362 printf ("\n ") if ($n % 4 eq 0);
363 ++$n;
364 printf (" [0x%04x] = 0x%04x,",
365 int(($k - 0xa1a1) / 256) * 94 + (($k - 0xa1a1) & 0xff), $u);
366 }
367 printf ("\n");
368
369*/
370

624/*
625
626 Mapping table from UCS4 to symbols defined in KS C 5601-1987.
627
628egrep '^0xA[1-C]' /cdrom/unix/mappings/eastasia/ksc/ksc5601.txt | \
629grep -v '# HANGUL SYLLABLE' | awk '{print $2, $1}' | sort -u |
630perl tab12.pl > ksc_sym2.tb
631
632 $n=0;
633 print " ";
634 while (<>) {
635 local($ucs4, $ksc, %rest) = split;
636 local($u)=hex($ucs4);
637 local($k)=hex($ksc);
638 local($ku)=int(($k - 0xa1a1) / 256) * 94 + (($k - 0xa1a1) & 0xff);
639 local($h)=0x21+int($ku/0x5e);
640 local($l)=0x21+int($ku%0x5e);
641 $n++;
642 printf (" {0x%04x, \"\\x%x\\x%x\"},", $u, $h, $l);
643 print "\n " if $n %3 == 0;
644 }
645 print "\n";
646
647*/
